GT Equivalence Verification (PO36)

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v
Candidate formulas: 54

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `0.156062620221068*sin(t) - 0.372947617362308*v*exp(-Abs(x))`.

The GT has two terms:
1. `F0*sin(t)` â€” a sine function of t only
2. `-beta*v*exp(-Abs(x))` â€” involves v times exp(-|x|)

The critical challenge is the `exp(-Abs(x))` term. Note that `exp(-|x|)` is NOT the same as `exp(c*x)` for any constant c, because |x| is not linear in x. For x > 0, exp(-|x|) = exp(-x), but for x < 0, exp(-|x|) = exp(x). No single `exp(c*x)` can match both behaviors.

Let me check each candidate for the ability to reproduce both terms.

**Term 1: sin(t)** â€” Most candidates have `c1*sin(c2 + c3*t)`, which with c2=0, c3=1 gives sin(t). This is fine.

**Term 2: v*exp(-|x|)** â€” This is the problematic term. Let me look for candidates that could handle this.

Most candidates have `c4*v*exp(c5*x)` which gives `v*exp(cx)` â€” this is exponential in x, not in |x|. This cannot match exp(-|x|) for all x.

Let me look for special candidates:

- **Candidate 28**: `c0*sin(c1 + c2*t) + c3*v*exp(c4*x)` â€” Just v*exp(cx), can't match.
- **Candidate 30**: Same structure, can't match.

None of the candidates contain `Abs(x)` or `|x|` in their expressions. Let me check if any candidate has a structure that could reproduce exp(-|x|).

Note that exp(-|x|) could potentially be built from combinations, but looking at the candidates, they all use polynomial or exponential functions of x (like exp(c*x), x**c, log terms, etc.), none of which can reproduce the non-analytic behavior of |x| at x=0.

Could any combination of terms work? For example:
- Two exponentials: `c*exp(a*x) + d*exp(b*x)` multiplied by v? Let me check candidates with two exp terms involving x.

**Candidate 48**: `c0 + c1*sin(c2 + c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*x) + c6*v*exp(c7*x)` â€” The c4*exp(c5*x) term doesn't have v, so it can't combine with the v*exp(c7*x) term to form v*exp(-|x|).

**Candidate 5**: `c0 + c1*sin(c2+c3*t) + c4*v + c5*v*x**2 + c6*v*exp(c7*x)` â€” polynomial + exponential in v, can't match.

**Candidate 44**: Has v*x and v*exp(c*x) terms, still can't match exp(-|x|).

**Candidate 6**: `c0*exp(c1*x) + c2*sin(c3*t+c4) + c5*v*x**c6 + c7*v*exp(c8*x)` â€” Has v*x^c6 + v*exp(c8*x), but x^c6 is not defined for negative x (in general), and still can't produce exp(-|x|).

**Candidate 32**: Has `log(c7*exp(c8*x + c9*v) + 1)` â€” this is a softplus-like function, not exp(-|x|).

No candidate has two `v*exp(c*x)` terms with different constants that could combine as:
`v*(a*exp(bx) + c*exp(dx))` to match `v*exp(-|x|)`.

Actually, even if a candidate had two such terms, `a*exp(bx) + c*exp(dx)` is smooth at x=0, while exp(-|x|) has a kink at x=0. So no finite sum of smooth functions of x can exactly equal exp(-|x|) for all x.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can reproduce the `exp(-Abs(x))` term, which is essential to match the GT. The function exp(-|x|) is non-analytic at x=0, and all candidate expressions are analytic in x (being composed of polynomials, exponentials of linear functions, logarithms, and trigonometric functions of x).
